  "content": "# Technical Report: Migration from Custom IPC to gRPC\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThis report provides a comprehensive architectural analysis of the SynestheticCanvas API Suite's inter-service communication system and outlines a phased migration plan from the current hybrid IPC/HTTP approach to gRPC. The analysis is based on examination of the codebase, including the `sc_ipc` library, API Gateway, microservices, and build configuration files.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Component Identification\n\n### 1.1 Current Inter-Service Communication Components\n\nThe SynestheticCanvas system uses a **hybrid communication approach**:\n\n1. **UNIX Domain Socket IPC Library (`sc_ipc`)** - for local inter-process communication\n2. **HTTP/REST over libcurl** - for network-based service-to-service calls\n\n#### Core IPC Library Files\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `libs/sc_ipc/include/sc_ipc.h` | Public API header defining the IPC interface, message types, error codes, and envelope structures |\n| `libs/sc_ipc/src/sc_ipc.c` | Implementation of UNIX domain socket-based IPC with length-prefixed framing |\n\n#### API Gateway Client-Side Communication\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `api-gateway/src/services/service_client.c` | HTTP/REST client wrapper using libcurl for communicating with downstream microservices |\n| `api-gateway/graphql/resolvers.c` | GraphQL resolvers that invoke `service_client` to call backend services |\n| `api-gateway/src/main.c` | Gateway entry point and HTTP server initialization |\n| `api-gateway/src/gateway_server.c` | HTTP server implementation |\n\n#### Microservice Server-Side Components\n\n| Service | Main Files |\n|---------|-----------|\n| **texture-service** | `services/texture-service/src/main.c` - HTTP daemon using libmicrohttpd |\n| | `services/texture-service/src/texture_handler.c` - Request handling and business logic |\n| | `services/texture-service/src/texture_service.c` - Core texture synthesis logic |\n| | `services/texture-service/src/texture_repository.c` - Data persistence layer |\n| **palette-service** | Similar structure in `services/palette-service/` |\n| **audio-service** | Similar structure in `services/audio-service/` |\n| **narrative-service** | Similar structure in `services/narrative-service/` |\n\n#### Shared Libraries\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `libs/sc_common/include/sc_config.h` | Runtime configuration, feature flags, environment variable parsing |\n| `libs/sc_common/include/sc_logging.h` | Structured logging utilities |\n| `libs/sc_common/include/sc_errors.h` | Error handling framework |\n| `libs/sc_common/include/sc_types.h` | Common type definitions |\n\n### 1.2 Current Communication Architecture\n\nBased on code analysis:\n\n1. **The `sc_ipc` library** provides UNIX domain socket communication with:\n   - Length-prefixed (4-byte big-endian) message framing\n   - Non-blocking I/O with configurable timeouts\n   - Server/client connection patterns\n   - Maximum 64KB payload size\n\n2. **The `service_client.c`** in the API Gateway uses:\n   - libcurl for HTTP/JSON REST calls to microservices\n   - Environment variables for service URLs (e.g., `SC_TEXTURE_SERVICE_URL`)\n   - Exponential backoff retry logic\n   - cJSON for JSON parsing\n\n3. **Microservices** expose HTTP endpoints via libmicrohttpd:\n   - REST endpoints like `/healthz`, `/v1/noise`\n   - JSON request/response format\n\n---\n\n## 2. Data Flow Analysis\n\n### 2.1 End-to-End Request Flow: API Gateway to Texture Service\n\nBased on the `data_flow.puml` and code analysis:\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510     HTTPS     \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510     HTTP/JSON    \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510     SQL     \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Client  \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6 \u2502 API Gateway \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6 \u2502 Texture Service \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6 \u2502 Database \u2502\n\u2502          \u2502              \u2502             \u2502                   \u2502                 \u2502             \u2502(Postgres)\u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518              \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518                   \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518             \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n#### Detailed Flow Sequence:\n\n1. **Client Request** (GraphQL or REST)\n   - Client sends HTTPS request to API Gateway\n   - Location: `api-gateway/src/main.c:196` (event loop)\n\n2. **Rate Limiting & Validation**\n   - Token bucket rate limiter checks quota (`rate_limit.h`)\n   - GraphQL schema validation via cgql library\n   - Location: `api-gateway/graphql/resolvers.c:194-196`\n\n3. **Resolver Execution**\n   - GraphQL runtime dispatches to appropriate resolver\n   - Example: `resolve_palette()` at `resolvers.c:184-210`\n\n4. **Service Client Call**\n   - `service_client.c:174-198` (`sc_service_client_call`)\n   - Builds full URL from endpoint base + path\n   - Makes HTTP request via libcurl with retry logic\n\n5. **Key Functions in Request Path:**\n   ```c\n   // API Gateway - resolvers.c\n   static json_t *resolve_palette(const json_t *args, void *user_data, GQLError **gql_err)\n\n   // API Gateway - service_client.c\n   int sc_service_client_call(sc_service_client_t *cli, sc_service_endp_t endpoint, ...)\n   static int perform_request(sc_service_client_t *client, const char *url, ...)\n\n   // Texture Service - main.c\n   static enum MHD_Result request_router(void *cls, struct MHD_Connection *connection, ...)\n\n   // Texture Service - texture_handler.c\n   Texture *texture_handler_get(TextureHandler *handler, const char *texture_id, TextureError *err)\n   ```\n\n6. **Response Path**\n   - Service returns JSON response\n   - Gateway parses and transforms to GraphQL response format\n   - Gateway caches response (Redis, optional TTL)\n   - Client receives final response\n\n#### Key Data Structures:\n\n```c\n// service_client.c\nstruct sc_service_client {\n    char *palette_url;\n    char *texture_url;\n    char *audio_url;\n    char *narrative_url;\n    long timeout_ms;\n    int max_retries;\n    atomic_ullong requests_total;\n    CURL *curl_handle;\n};\n\n// sc_ipc.h (for future reference)\ntypedef struct sc_ipc_msg_hdr {\n    uint32_t magic;           // 0xC0FEBABE\n    uint16_t version;\n    uint16_t type;            // REQUEST, RESPONSE, EVENT, HEARTBEAT\n    uint32_t length;\n    uint64_t correlation_id;\n    uint64_t timestamp_ns;\n} sc_ipc_msg_hdr_t;\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Migration Strategy Proposal\n\n### 3.1 Phase 1: Foundation (Weeks 1-2)\n\n#### 3.1.1 Define gRPC Service Contracts\n\nCreate Protocol Buffer definitions for the texture service:\n\n```protobuf\n// proto/texture.proto\nsyntax = \"proto3\";\n\npackage synestheticcanvas.texture.v1;\n\nservice TextureService {\n    rpc GetTexture(GetTextureRequest) returns (GetTextureResponse);\n    rpc CreateTexture(CreateTextureRequest) returns (CreateTextureResponse);\n    rpc ListTextures(ListTexturesRequest) returns (ListTexturesResponse);\n    rpc DeleteTexture(DeleteTextureRequest) returns (DeleteTextureResponse);\n    rpc GenerateNoise(GenerateNoiseRequest) returns (GenerateNoiseResponse);\n}\n\nmessage GetTextureRequest {\n    string texture_id = 1;\n}\n\nmessage GetTextureResponse {\n    Texture texture = 1;\n}\n\nmessage Texture {\n    string id = 1;\n    string name = 2;\n    string color_profile = 3;\n    uint32 width = 4;\n    uint32 height = 5;\n    uint64 created_at = 6;\n}\n\n// ... additional message definitions\n```\n\n#### 3.1.2 CMakeLists.txt Modifications\n\n**For the texture-service (`services/texture-service/CMakeLists.txt`):**\n\n```cmake\n# Add gRPC/Protobuf dependencies\nfind_package(Protobuf REQUIRED)\nfind_package(gRPC CONFIG REQUIRED)\n\n# Generate C sources from .proto files\nset(PROTO_SRC_DIR ${CMAKE_CURRENT_SOURCE_DIR}/proto)\nset(PROTO_FILES ${PROTO_SRC_DIR}/texture.proto)\n\n# Use protoc and grpc_cpp_plugin\nadd_custom_command(\n    OUTPUT texture.pb.c texture.pb-c.h texture.grpc.pb.c texture.grpc.pb-c.h\n    COMMAND ${Protobuf_PROTOC_EXECUTABLE}\n    ARGS --c_out=${CMAKE_CURRENT_BINARY_DIR}\n         --grpc_out=${CMAKE_CURRENT_BINARY_DIR}\n         --plugin=protoc-gen-grpc=${gRPC_CPP_PLUGIN_EXECUTABLE}\n         -I${PROTO_SRC_DIR}\n         ${PROTO_FILES}\n    DEPENDS ${PROTO_FILES}\n)\n\n# Add generated files to sources\nset(GRPC_GENERATED_SRC\n    ${CMAKE_CURRENT_BINARY_DIR}/texture.pb.c\n    ${CMAKE_CURRENT_BINARY_DIR}/texture.grpc.pb.c\n)\n\ntarget_sources(texture_service PRIVATE ${GRPC_GENERATED_SRC})\ntarget_link_libraries(texture_service\n    PUBLIC\n        gRPC::grpc\n        protobuf::libprotobuf-c\n)\n```\n\n**For the API Gateway (`api-gateway/CMakeLists.txt`):**\n\n```cmake\n# Add gRPC client dependencies\nfind_package(gRPC CONFIG REQUIRED)\nfind_package(Protobuf REQUIRED)\n\n# Include generated protobuf headers\ntarget_include_directories(api_gateway PRIVATE ${CMAKE_BINARY_DIR}/generated)\n\n# Link gRPC client library\ntarget_link_libraries(api_gateway\n    PRIVATE\n        gRPC::grpc\n        protobuf::libprotobuf-c\n)\n```\n\n### 3.2 Phase 2: Parallel Implementation (Weeks 3-4)\n\n#### 3.2.1 Dual-Protocol Server in Texture Service\n\nModify `services/texture-service/src/main.c` to support both HTTP and gRPC simultaneously:\n\n```c\n// main.c - Conceptual structure for dual-protocol support\n#include <grpc/grpc.h>\n#include <microhttpd.h>\n\ntypedef struct {\n    struct MHD_Daemon *http_daemon;  // Existing HTTP server\n    grpc_server *grpc_server;        // New gRPC server\n    ServiceConfig cfg;\n} DualServiceCtx;\n\n// gRPC handler (new)\nstatic grpc_call_error handle_grpc_get_texture(\n    grpc_call *call,\n    GetTextureRequest *req,\n    GetTextureResponse **resp\n) {\n    // Reuse existing handler logic\n    TextureError err = {0};\n    Texture *tx = texture_handler_get(g_handler, req->texture_id, &err);\n    if (!tx) {\n        return grpc_call_error_from_texture_error(&err);\n    }\n    *resp = texture_to_grpc_response(tx);\n    texture_free(tx);\n    return GRPC_CALL_OK;\n}\n\nint main(void)\n{\n    DualServiceCtx svc;\n    config_set_defaults(&svc.cfg);\n\n    // Start HTTP daemon on default port (existing)\n    svc.http_daemon = MHD_start_daemon(\n        MHD_USE_AUTO | MHD_USE_INTERNAL_POLLING_THREAD,\n        svc.cfg.port,\n        NULL, NULL,\n        request_router, &svc,\n        MHD_OPTION_END\n    );\n\n    // Start gRPC server on separate port (new)\n    uint16_t grpc_port = svc.cfg.port + 1000;  // e.g., 9080 if HTTP is 8080\n    svc.grpc_server = grpc_server_create(NULL, NULL);\n    grpc_server_add_http2_port(svc.grpc_server,\n        format_address(\"0.0.0.0\", grpc_port),\n        grpc_insecure_server_credentials_create());\n\n    grpc_server_register_method(svc.grpc_server,\n        \"/texture.v1.TextureService/GetTexture\",\n        handle_grpc_get_texture);\n\n    grpc_server_start(svc.grpc_server);\n\n    log_msg(LOG_INFO, \"Dual-protocol server: HTTP=%u, gRPC=%u\",\n            svc.cfg.port, grpc_port);\n\n    // Event loop handles both...\n    while (!g_shutdown) sleep(1);\n\n    // Graceful shutdown\n    MHD_stop_daemon(svc.http_daemon);\n    grpc_server_shutdown_and_notify(svc.grpc_server, NULL, NULL);\n    grpc_server_destroy(svc.grpc_server);\n\n    return EXIT_SUCCESS;\n}\n```\n\n#### 3.2.2 Feature Flag in API Gateway Configuration\n\nExtend `sc_config.h` and `service_client.c`:\n\n```c\n// In sc_config.h - add feature toggle\n#ifndef SC_FEATURE_GRPC_TEXTURE\n#   define SC_FEATURE_GRPC_TEXTURE 0  // Off by default during migration\n#endif\n\n// Environment variable override\nstatic inline bool sc_use_grpc_for_service(const char *service_name) {\n    char env_var[64];\n    snprintf(env_var, sizeof(env_var), \"SC_USE_GRPC_%s\", service_name);\n    return sc_bool_from_env(env_var, false);\n}\n```\n\n```c\n// In service_client.c - protocol selection logic\nint sc_service_client_call(sc_service_client_t *cli,\n                           sc_service_endp_t endpoint,\n                           const char *method,\n                           const char *path,\n                           const char *request_json,\n                           cJSON **response_json,\n                           long *http_status)\n{\n    // Check if gRPC is enabled for this service\n    if (endpoint == SC_EP_TEXTURE && sc_use_grpc_for_service(\"TEXTURE\")) {\n        return sc_service_client_call_grpc(cli, endpoint, method, path,\n                                           request_json, response_json, http_status);\n    }\n\n    // Fallback to existing HTTP/REST implementation\n    return sc_service_client_call_http(cli, endpoint, method, path,\n                                       request_json, response_json, http_status);\n}\n```\n\n### 3.3 Phase 3: Gradual Rollout (Weeks 5-6)\n\n#### 3.3.1 Deployment Strategy\n\n1. **Canary Deployment**\n   - Deploy texture-service with dual-protocol support\n   - Set `SC_USE_GRPC_TEXTURE=false` initially\n   - Route 5% of traffic to gRPC via feature flag\n\n2. **Incremental Traffic Shift**\n   - Week 5: 5% \u2192 25% \u2192 50%\n   - Week 6: 75% \u2192 100%\n   - Monitor latency, error rates, resource usage\n\n3. **Rollback Capability**\n   - `SC_USE_GRPC_TEXTURE=false` instantly reverts to HTTP\n   - No service restart required\n\n### 3.4 Phase 4: Consolidation (Weeks 7-8)\n\n1. Remove HTTP endpoints from texture-service\n2. Update API Gateway to use gRPC exclusively for texture-service\n3. Remove dual-protocol code, simplify to gRPC-only\n4. Repeat phases 2-4 for remaining services (palette, audio, narrative)\n\n### 3.5 New gRPC-Based Communication Flow\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510   GraphQL/REST   \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510      gRPC/HTTP/2      \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Client  \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6 \u2502 API Gateway \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6 \u2502 Texture Service \u2502\n\u2502          \u2502                  \u2502             \u2502                        \u2502                 \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518                  \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518                        \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                                    \u2502\n                                    \u2502 Protocol Buffer\n                                    \u2502 serialization\n                                    \u25bc\n                              \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n                              \u2502 gRPC Client \u2502\n                              \u2502   Stub      \u2502\n                              \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n**Key Changes:**\n- Binary Protocol Buffers replace JSON serialization\n- HTTP/2 enables multiplexed streaming\n- Strongly-typed service contracts via `.proto` files\n- Built-in load balancing and service discovery options\n\n---\n\n## 4. Risk Assessment\n\n### 4.1 Build System Complexity (HIGH RISK)\n\n**Risk:** Integrating gRPC into a C project via CMake is non-trivial.\n\n**Details:**\n- gRPC's primary support is for C++, not C. The C bindings (gRPC Core) have limited documentation.\n- Protobuf code generation requires `protobuf-c` (a third-party C protobuf library), not the official Google `protobuf`.\n- FetchContent patterns for gRPC often fail due to complex transitive dependencies (abseil, re2, etc.).\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Use system-installed gRPC packages (`apt install libgrpc-dev`) rather than FetchContent\n- Consider gRPC-C alternatives like `grpc_c` or `protobuf-c-rpc`\n- Extensive pre-merge CI testing of the build system changes\n\n**Evidence from codebase:**\n- Current CMakeLists.txt files use FetchContent for simple dependencies (cJSON, libgraphqlparser)\n- No existing gRPC usage means no precedent for integration patterns\n\n### 4.2 Performance Characteristics (MEDIUM RISK)\n\n**Risk:** gRPC may introduce latency overhead compared to the custom IPC.\n\n**Details:**\n- The current `sc_ipc` library uses UNIX domain sockets with a lean 4-byte length-prefix framing\n- gRPC adds HTTP/2 framing, Protobuf encoding/decoding, and connection management overhead\n- For intra-host communication, UNIX sockets typically outperform TCP-based gRPC\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Benchmark before/after migration (target: <10% latency increase)\n- Consider gRPC over UNIX domain sockets for intra-host calls\n- Use connection pooling and keep-alive to reduce handshake overhead\n\n**Evidence from codebase:**\n- `sc_ipc.h:62-64` specifies max 64KB payloads and UNIX domain socket transport\n- Performance target from `overview.md:17`: \"Frame-accurate (< 16 ms) responses\"\n\n### 4.3 Operational Complexity During Transition (MEDIUM RISK)\n\n**Risk:** Running dual-protocol systems increases operational burden.\n\n**Details:**\n- Configuration management doubles (HTTP endpoints + gRPC ports)\n- Monitoring/alerting must cover both protocols\n- Load balancers need updating (gRPC requires HTTP/2-aware proxying)\n- Service discovery must track additional endpoints\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Use environment variables with sensible defaults\n- Implement health checks for both protocols\n- Phase transition quickly (6-8 weeks target)\n- Document operational runbooks for both modes\n\n**Evidence from codebase:**\n- Service configuration via environment variables (`sc_config.h:204-215`)\n- Health endpoint pattern: `/healthz` returns `{\"status\":\"ok\"}` (`main.c:289-294`)\n\n### 4.4 Code Divergence Risk (MEDIUM RISK)\n\n**Risk:** Maintaining two code paths during migration introduces bugs.\n\n**Details:**\n- Handler logic may drift between HTTP and gRPC implementations\n- Testing burden doubles\n- Edge case handling may differ\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Extract business logic into protocol-agnostic functions\n- Comprehensive integration tests covering both paths\n- Short migration window to minimize divergence period\n\n**Evidence from codebase:**\n- Handler logic in `texture_handler.c` is already separated from transport\n- Repository pattern (`texture_repository.c`) enables clean abstraction\n\n### 4.5 Language Ecosystem Friction (LOW-MEDIUM RISK)\n\n**Risk:** gRPC's C ecosystem is less mature than C++ or Go.\n\n**Details:**\n- gRPC Core's C API is marked as \"low-level\" and \"for advanced users\"\n- Documentation focuses on C++, Python, and Go\n- Fewer community examples and Stack Overflow answers\n- May need to drop to gRPC Core primitives for advanced features\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Consider a C++ wrapper layer if C API proves too cumbersome\n- Evaluate alternatives like Cap'n Proto or FlatBuffers with RPC\n- Budget extra time for learning curve\n\n**Evidence from documentation:**\n- `microservices.md` references gRPC but with C++ style (`gen/palette.grpc.pb-c.h`)\n- Current code uses C11/C17 standards without C++ dependencies\n\n---\n\n## 5. Recommendations\n\n### 5.1 Immediate Actions\n\n1. **Proof of Concept:** Build a minimal gRPC server in C for the texture service to validate CMake integration\n2. **Benchmark Baseline:** Measure current HTTP latency, throughput, and resource usage\n3. **Define Proto Contracts:** Create `.proto` files for all four services before implementation begins\n\n### 5.2 Technical Decisions\n\n1. **Use `grpc-c` or gRPC Core + protobuf-c** for C compatibility\n2. **Keep HTTP as fallback** even post-migration for debugging and legacy clients\n3. **Implement gRPC reflection** to enable tools like `grpcurl` for debugging\n\n### 5.3 Success Criteria\n\n| Metric | Target |\n|--------|--------|\n| P95 Latency | < 20ms (max 25% increase from baseline) |\n| Error Rate | < 0.1% during rollout |\n| Migration Duration | < 8 weeks per service |\n| Build Time Increase | < 20% |\n\n---\n\n## 6. Appendix: File Reference Summary\n\n### IPC/Communication Layer\n- `libs/sc_ipc/include/sc_ipc.h` - IPC API (lines 1-207)\n- `libs/sc_ipc/src/sc_ipc.c` - IPC implementation (lines 1-443)\n- `api-gateway/src/services/service_client.c` - HTTP client (lines 1-359)\n\n### API Gateway\n- `api-gateway/graphql/resolvers.c` - GraphQL resolvers (lines 1-408)\n- `api-gateway/src/main.c` - Gateway entry point\n- `api-gateway/CMakeLists.txt` - Build configuration (lines 1-281)\n\n### Texture Service (Representative Microservice)\n- `services/texture-service/src/main.c` - Service entry point (lines 1-438)\n- `services/texture-service/src/texture_handler.c` - Request handlers (lines 1-400)\n- `services/texture-service/CMakeLists.txt` - Build configuration (lines 1-248)\n\n### Configuration/Common\n- `libs/sc_common/include/sc_config.h` - Configuration framework (lines 1-303)\n- `docs/architecture/data_flow.puml` - Architecture diagram (lines 1-172)\n- `docs/architecture/overview.md` - System overview (lines 1-299)\n- `docs/architecture/microservices.md` - Microservices documentation (lines 1-572)\n\n---\n\n*Report prepared based on codebase analysis of SynestheticCanvas API Suite v1.4.x*\n",

  "content": "# Technical Report: Migration from Custom IPC to gRPC\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThis report provides a comprehensive architectural analysis of the SynestheticCanvas API Suite's inter-service communication system and outlines a phased migration plan from the current hybrid IPC/HTTP approach to gRPC. The analysis is based on examination of the codebase, including the `sc_ipc` library, API Gateway, microservices, and build configuration files.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Component Identification\n\n### 1.1 Current Inter-Service Communication Components\n\nThe SynestheticCanvas system uses a **hybrid communication approach**:\n\n1. **UNIX Domain Socket IPC Library (`sc_ipc`)** - for local inter-process communication\n2. **HTTP/REST over libcurl** - for network-based service-to-service calls\n\n#### Core IPC Library Files\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `libs/sc_ipc/include/sc_ipc.h` | Public API header defining the IPC interface, message types, error codes, and envelope structures |\n| `libs/sc_ipc/src/sc_ipc.c` | Implementation of UNIX domain socket-based IPC with length-prefixed framing |\n\n#### API Gateway Client-Side Communication\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `api-gateway/src/services/service_client.c` | HTTP/REST client wrapper using libcurl for communicating with downstream microservices |\n| `api-gateway/graphql/resolvers.c` | GraphQL resolvers that invoke `service_client` to call backend services |\n| `api-gateway/src/main.c` | Gateway entry point and HTTP server initialization |\n| `api-gateway/src/gateway_server.c` | HTTP server implementation |\n\n#### Microservice Server-Side Components\n\n| Service | Main Files |\n|---------|-----------|\n| **texture-service** | `services/texture-service/src/main.c` - HTTP daemon using libmicrohttpd |\n| | `services/texture-service/src/texture_handler.c` - Request handling and business logic |\n| | `services/texture-service/src/texture_service.c` - Core texture synthesis logic |\n| | `services/texture-service/src/texture_repository.c` - Data persistence layer |\n| **palette-service** | Similar structure in `services/palette-service/` |\n| **audio-service** | Similar structure in `services/audio-service/` |\n| **narrative-service** | Similar structure in `services/narrative-service/` |\n\n#### Shared Libraries\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `libs/sc_common/include/sc_config.h` | Runtime configuration, feature flags, environment variable parsing |\n| `libs/sc_common/include/sc_logging.h` | Structured logging utilities |\n| `libs/sc_common/include/sc_errors.h` | Error handling framework |\n| `libs/sc_common/include/sc_types.h` | Common type definitions |\n\n### 1.2 Current Communication Architecture\n\nBased on code analysis:\n\n1. **The `sc_ipc` library** provides UNIX domain socket communication with:\n   - Length-prefixed (4-byte big-endian) message framing\n   - Non-blocking I/O with configurable timeouts\n   - Server/client connection patterns\n   - Maximum 64KB payload size\n\n2. **The `service_client.c`** in the API Gateway uses:\n   - libcurl for HTTP/JSON REST calls to microservices\n   - Environment variables for service URLs (e.g., `SC_TEXTURE_SERVICE_URL`)\n   - Exponential backoff retry logic\n   - cJSON for JSON parsing\n\n3. **Microservices** expose HTTP endpoints via libmicrohttpd:\n   - REST endpoints like `/healthz`, `/v1/noise`\n   - JSON request/response format\n\n---\n\n## 2. Data Flow Analysis\n\n### 2.1 End-to-End Request Flow: API Gateway to Texture Service\n\nBased on the `data_flow.puml` and code analysis:\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510     HTTPS     \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510     HTTP/JSON    \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510     SQL     \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Client  \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6 \u2502 API Gateway \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6 \u2502 Texture Service \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6 \u2502 Database \u2502\n\u2502          \u2502              \u2502             \u2502                   \u2502                 \u2502             \u2502(Postgres)\u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518              \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518                   \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518             \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n#### Detailed Flow Sequence:\n\n1. **Client Request** (GraphQL or REST)\n   - Client sends HTTPS request to API Gateway\n   - Location: `api-gateway/src/main.c:196` (event loop)\n\n2. **Rate Limiting & Validation**\n   - Token bucket rate limiter checks quota (`rate_limit.h`)\n   - GraphQL schema validation via cgql library\n   - Location: `api-gateway/graphql/resolvers.c:194-196`\n\n3. **Resolver Execution**\n   - GraphQL runtime dispatches to appropriate resolver\n   - Example: `resolve_palette()` at `resolvers.c:184-210`\n\n4. **Service Client Call**\n   - `service_client.c:174-198` (`sc_service_client_call`)\n   - Builds full URL from endpoint base + path\n   - Makes HTTP request via libcurl with retry logic\n\n5. **Key Functions in Request Path:**\n   ```c\n   // API Gateway - resolvers.c\n   static json_t *resolve_palette(const json_t *args, void *user_data, GQLError **gql_err)\n\n   // API Gateway - service_client.c\n   int sc_service_client_call(sc_service_client_t *cli, sc_service_endp_t endpoint, ...)\n   static int perform_request(sc_service_client_t *client, const char *url, ...)\n\n   // Texture Service - main.c\n   static enum MHD_Result request_router(void *cls, struct MHD_Connection *connection, ...)\n\n   // Texture Service - texture_handler.c\n   Texture *texture_handler_get(TextureHandler *handler, const char *texture_id, TextureError *err)\n   ```\n\n6. **Response Path**\n   - Service returns JSON response\n   - Gateway parses and transforms to GraphQL response format\n   - Gateway caches response (Redis, optional TTL)\n   - Client receives final response\n\n#### Key Data Structures:\n\n```c\n// service_client.c\nstruct sc_service_client {\n    char *palette_url;\n    char *texture_url;\n    char *audio_url;\n    char *narrative_url;\n    long timeout_ms;\n    int max_retries;\n    atomic_ullong requests_total;\n    CURL *curl_handle;\n};\n\n// sc_ipc.h (for future reference)\ntypedef struct sc_ipc_msg_hdr {\n    uint32_t magic;           // 0xC0FEBABE\n    uint16_t version;\n    uint16_t type;            // REQUEST, RESPONSE, EVENT, HEARTBEAT\n    uint32_t length;\n    uint64_t correlation_id;\n    uint64_t timestamp_ns;\n} sc_ipc_msg_hdr_t;\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Migration Strategy Proposal\n\n### 3.1 Phase 1: Foundation (Weeks 1-2)\n\n#### 3.1.1 Define gRPC Service Contracts\n\nCreate Protocol Buffer definitions for the texture service:\n\n```protobuf\n// proto/texture.proto\nsyntax = \"proto3\";\n\npackage synestheticcanvas.texture.v1;\n\nservice TextureService {\n    rpc GetTexture(GetTextureRequest) returns (GetTextureResponse);\n    rpc CreateTexture(CreateTextureRequest) returns (CreateTextureResponse);\n    rpc ListTextures(ListTexturesRequest) returns (ListTexturesResponse);\n    rpc DeleteTexture(DeleteTextureRequest) returns (DeleteTextureResponse);\n    rpc GenerateNoise(GenerateNoiseRequest) returns (GenerateNoiseResponse);\n}\n\nmessage GetTextureRequest {\n    string texture_id = 1;\n}\n\nmessage GetTextureResponse {\n    Texture texture = 1;\n}\n\nmessage Texture {\n    string id = 1;\n    string name = 2;\n    string color_profile = 3;\n    uint32 width = 4;\n    uint32 height = 5;\n    uint64 created_at = 6;\n}\n\n// ... additional message definitions\n```\n\n#### 3.1.2 CMakeLists.txt Modifications\n\n**For the texture-service (`services/texture-service/CMakeLists.txt`):**\n\n```cmake\n# Add gRPC/Protobuf dependencies\nfind_package(Protobuf REQUIRED)\nfind_package(gRPC CONFIG REQUIRED)\n\n# Generate C sources from .proto files\nset(PROTO_SRC_DIR ${CMAKE_CURRENT_SOURCE_DIR}/proto)\nset(PROTO_FILES ${PROTO_SRC_DIR}/texture.proto)\n\n# Use protoc and grpc_cpp_plugin\nadd_custom_command(\n    OUTPUT texture.pb.c texture.pb-c.h texture.grpc.pb.c texture.grpc.pb-c.h\n    COMMAND ${Protobuf_PROTOC_EXECUTABLE}\n    ARGS --c_out=${CMAKE_CURRENT_BINARY_DIR}\n         --grpc_out=${CMAKE_CURRENT_BINARY_DIR}\n         --plugin=protoc-gen-grpc=${gRPC_CPP_PLUGIN_EXECUTABLE}\n         -I${PROTO_SRC_DIR}\n         ${PROTO_FILES}\n    DEPENDS ${PROTO_FILES}\n)\n\n# Add generated files to sources\nset(GRPC_GENERATED_SRC\n    ${CMAKE_CURRENT_BINARY_DIR}/texture.pb.c\n    ${CMAKE_CURRENT_BINARY_DIR}/texture.grpc.pb.c\n)\n\ntarget_sources(texture_service PRIVATE ${GRPC_GENERATED_SRC})\ntarget_link_libraries(texture_service\n    PUBLIC\n        gRPC::grpc\n        protobuf::libprotobuf-c\n)\n```\n\n**For the API Gateway (`api-gateway/CMakeLists.txt`):**\n\n```cmake\n# Add gRPC client dependencies\nfind_package(gRPC CONFIG REQUIRED)\nfind_package(Protobuf REQUIRED)\n\n# Include generated protobuf headers\ntarget_include_directories(api_gateway PRIVATE ${CMAKE_BINARY_DIR}/generated)\n\n# Link gRPC client library\ntarget_link_libraries(api_gateway\n    PRIVATE\n        gRPC::grpc\n        protobuf::libprotobuf-c\n)\n```\n\n### 3.2 Phase 2: Parallel Implementation (Weeks 3-4)\n\n#### 3.2.1 Dual-Protocol Server in Texture Service\n\nModify `services/texture-service/src/main.c` to support both HTTP and gRPC simultaneously:\n\n```c\n// main.c - Conceptual structure for dual-protocol support\n#include <grpc/grpc.h>\n#include <microhttpd.h>\n\ntypedef struct {\n    struct MHD_Daemon *http_daemon;  // Existing HTTP server\n    grpc_server *grpc_server;        // New gRPC server\n    ServiceConfig cfg;\n} DualServiceCtx;\n\n// gRPC handler (new)\nstatic grpc_call_error handle_grpc_get_texture(\n    grpc_call *call,\n    GetTextureRequest *req,\n    GetTextureResponse **resp\n) {\n    // Reuse existing handler logic\n    TextureError err = {0};\n    Texture *tx = texture_handler_get(g_handler, req->texture_id, &err);\n    if (!tx) {\n        return grpc_call_error_from_texture_error(&err);\n    }\n    *resp = texture_to_grpc_response(tx);\n    texture_free(tx);\n    return GRPC_CALL_OK;\n}\n\nint main(void)\n{\n    DualServiceCtx svc;\n    config_set_defaults(&svc.cfg);\n\n    // Start HTTP daemon on default port (existing)\n    svc.http_daemon = MHD_start_daemon(\n        MHD_USE_AUTO | MHD_USE_INTERNAL_POLLING_THREAD,\n        svc.cfg.port,\n        NULL, NULL,\n        request_router, &svc,\n        MHD_OPTION_END\n    );\n\n    // Start gRPC server on separate port (new)\n    uint16_t grpc_port = svc.cfg.port + 1000;  // e.g., 9080 if HTTP is 8080\n    svc.grpc_server = grpc_server_create(NULL, NULL);\n    grpc_server_add_http2_port(svc.grpc_server,\n        format_address(\"0.0.0.0\", grpc_port),\n        grpc_insecure_server_credentials_create());\n\n    grpc_server_register_method(svc.grpc_server,\n        \"/texture.v1.TextureService/GetTexture\",\n        handle_grpc_get_texture);\n\n    grpc_server_start(svc.grpc_server);\n\n    log_msg(LOG_INFO, \"Dual-protocol server: HTTP=%u, gRPC=%u\",\n            svc.cfg.port, grpc_port);\n\n    // Event loop handles both...\n    while (!g_shutdown) sleep(1);\n\n    // Graceful shutdown\n    MHD_stop_daemon(svc.http_daemon);\n    grpc_server_shutdown_and_notify(svc.grpc_server, NULL, NULL);\n    grpc_server_destroy(svc.grpc_server);\n\n    return EXIT_SUCCESS;\n}\n```\n\n#### 3.2.2 Feature Flag in API Gateway Configuration\n\nExtend `sc_config.h` and `service_client.c`:\n\n```c\n// In sc_config.h - add feature toggle\n#ifndef SC_FEATURE_GRPC_TEXTURE\n#   define SC_FEATURE_GRPC_TEXTURE 0  // Off by default during migration\n#endif\n\n// Environment variable override\nstatic inline bool sc_use_grpc_for_service(const char *service_name) {\n    char env_var[64];\n    snprintf(env_var, sizeof(env_var), \"SC_USE_GRPC_%s\", service_name);\n    return sc_bool_from_env(env_var, false);\n}\n```\n\n```c\n// In service_client.c - protocol selection logic\nint sc_service_client_call(sc_service_client_t *cli,\n                           sc_service_endp_t endpoint,\n                           const char *method,\n                           const char *path,\n                           const char *request_json,\n                           cJSON **response_json,\n                           long *http_status)\n{\n    // Check if gRPC is enabled for this service\n    if (endpoint == SC_EP_TEXTURE && sc_use_grpc_for_service(\"TEXTURE\")) {\n        return sc_service_client_call_grpc(cli, endpoint, method, path,\n                                           request_json, response_json, http_status);\n    }\n\n    // Fallback to existing HTTP/REST implementation\n    return sc_service_client_call_http(cli, endpoint, method, path,\n                                       request_json, response_json, http_status);\n}\n```\n\n### 3.3 Phase 3: Gradual Rollout (Weeks 5-6)\n\n#### 3.3.1 Deployment Strategy\n\n1. **Canary Deployment**\n   - Deploy texture-service with dual-protocol support\n   - Set `SC_USE_GRPC_TEXTURE=false` initially\n   - Route 5% of traffic to gRPC via feature flag\n\n2. **Incremental Traffic Shift**\n   - Week 5: 5% \u2192 25% \u2192 50%\n   - Week 6: 75% \u2192 100%\n   - Monitor latency, error rates, resource usage\n\n3. **Rollback Capability**\n   - `SC_USE_GRPC_TEXTURE=false` instantly reverts to HTTP\n   - No service restart required\n\n### 3.4 Phase 4: Consolidation (Weeks 7-8)\n\n1. Remove HTTP endpoints from texture-service\n2. Update API Gateway to use gRPC exclusively for texture-service\n3. Remove dual-protocol code, simplify to gRPC-only\n4. Repeat phases 2-4 for remaining services (palette, audio, narrative)\n\n### 3.5 New gRPC-Based Communication Flow\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510   GraphQL/REST   \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510      gRPC/HTTP/2      \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Client  \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6 \u2502 API Gateway \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6 \u2502 Texture Service \u2502\n\u2502          \u2502                  \u2502             \u2502                        \u2502                 \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518                  \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518                        \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                                    \u2502\n                                    \u2502 Protocol Buffer\n                                    \u2502 serialization\n                                    \u25bc\n                              \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n                              \u2502 gRPC Client \u2502\n                              \u2502   Stub      \u2502\n                              \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n**Key Changes:**\n- Binary Protocol Buffers replace JSON serialization\n- HTTP/2 enables multiplexed streaming\n- Strongly-typed service contracts via `.proto` files\n- Built-in load balancing and service discovery options\n\n---\n\n## 4. Risk Assessment\n\n### 4.1 Build System Complexity (HIGH RISK)\n\n**Risk:** Integrating gRPC into a C project via CMake is non-trivial.\n\n**Details:**\n- gRPC's primary support is for C++, not C. The C bindings (gRPC Core) have limited documentation.\n- Protobuf code generation requires `protobuf-c` (a third-party C protobuf library), not the official Google `protobuf`.\n- FetchContent patterns for gRPC often fail due to complex transitive dependencies (abseil, re2, etc.).\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Use system-installed gRPC packages (`apt install libgrpc-dev`) rather than FetchContent\n- Consider gRPC-C alternatives like `grpc_c` or `protobuf-c-rpc`\n- Extensive pre-merge CI testing of the build system changes\n\n**Evidence from codebase:**\n- Current CMakeLists.txt files use FetchContent for simple dependencies (cJSON, libgraphqlparser)\n- No existing gRPC usage means no precedent for integration patterns\n\n### 4.2 Performance Characteristics (MEDIUM RISK)\n\n**Risk:** gRPC may introduce latency overhead compared to the custom IPC.\n\n**Details:**\n- The current `sc_ipc` library uses UNIX domain sockets with a lean 4-byte length-prefix framing\n- gRPC adds HTTP/2 framing, Protobuf encoding/decoding, and connection management overhead\n- For intra-host communication, UNIX sockets typically outperform TCP-based gRPC\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Benchmark before/after migration (target: <10% latency increase)\n- Consider gRPC over UNIX domain sockets for intra-host calls\n- Use connection pooling and keep-alive to reduce handshake overhead\n\n**Evidence from codebase:**\n- `sc_ipc.h:62-64` specifies max 64KB payloads and UNIX domain socket transport\n- Performance target from `overview.md:17`: \"Frame-accurate (< 16 ms) responses\"\n\n### 4.3 Operational Complexity During Transition (MEDIUM RISK)\n\n**Risk:** Running dual-protocol systems increases operational burden.\n\n**Details:**\n- Configuration management doubles (HTTP endpoints + gRPC ports)\n- Monitoring/alerting must cover both protocols\n- Load balancers need updating (gRPC requires HTTP/2-aware proxying)\n- Service discovery must track additional endpoints\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Use environment variables with sensible defaults\n- Implement health checks for both protocols\n- Phase transition quickly (6-8 weeks target)\n- Document operational runbooks for both modes\n\n**Evidence from codebase:**\n- Service configuration via environment variables (`sc_config.h:204-215`)\n- Health endpoint pattern: `/healthz` returns `{\"status\":\"ok\"}` (`main.c:289-294`)\n\n### 4.4 Code Divergence Risk (MEDIUM RISK)\n\n**Risk:** Maintaining two code paths during migration introduces bugs.\n\n**Details:**\n- Handler logic may drift between HTTP and gRPC implementations\n- Testing burden doubles\n- Edge case handling may differ\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Extract business logic into protocol-agnostic functions\n- Comprehensive integration tests covering both paths\n- Short migration window to minimize divergence period\n\n**Evidence from codebase:**\n- Handler logic in `texture_handler.c` is already separated from transport\n- Repository pattern (`texture_repository.c`) enables clean abstraction\n\n### 4.5 Language Ecosystem Friction (LOW-MEDIUM RISK)\n\n**Risk:** gRPC's C ecosystem is less mature than C++ or Go.\n\n**Details:**\n- gRPC Core's C API is marked as \"low-level\" and \"for advanced users\"\n- Documentation focuses on C++, Python, and Go\n- Fewer community examples and Stack Overflow answers\n- May need to drop to gRPC Core primitives for advanced features\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Consider a C++ wrapper layer if C API proves too cumbersome\n- Evaluate alternatives like Cap'n Proto or FlatBuffers with RPC\n- Budget extra time for learning curve\n\n**Evidence from documentation:**\n- `microservices.md` references gRPC but with C++ style (`gen/palette.grpc.pb-c.h`)\n- Current code uses C11/C17 standards without C++ dependencies\n\n---\n\n## 5. Recommendations\n\n### 5.1 Immediate Actions\n\n1. **Proof of Concept:** Build a minimal gRPC server in C for the texture service to validate CMake integration\n2. **Benchmark Baseline:** Measure current HTTP latency, throughput, and resource usage\n3. **Define Proto Contracts:** Create `.proto` files for all four services before implementation begins\n\n### 5.2 Technical Decisions\n\n1. **Use `grpc-c` or gRPC Core + protobuf-c** for C compatibility\n2. **Keep HTTP as fallback** even post-migration for debugging and legacy clients\n3. **Implement gRPC reflection** to enable tools like `grpcurl` for debugging\n\n### 5.3 Success Criteria\n\n| Metric | Target |\n|--------|--------|\n| P95 Latency | < 20ms (max 25% increase from baseline) |\n| Error Rate | < 0.1% during rollout |\n| Migration Duration | < 8 weeks per service |\n| Build Time Increase | < 20% |\n\n---\n\n## 6. Appendix: File Reference Summary\n\n### IPC/Communication Layer\n- `libs/sc_ipc/include/sc_ipc.h` - IPC API (lines 1-207)\n- `libs/sc_ipc/src/sc_ipc.c` - IPC implementation (lines 1-443)\n- `api-gateway/src/services/service_client.c` - HTTP client (lines 1-359)\n\n### API Gateway\n- `api-gateway/graphql/resolvers.c` - GraphQL resolvers (lines 1-408)\n- `api-gateway/src/main.c` - Gateway entry point\n- `api-gateway/CMakeLists.txt` - Build configuration (lines 1-281)\n\n### Texture Service (Representative Microservice)\n- `services/texture-service/src/main.c` - Service entry point (lines 1-438)\n- `services/texture-service/src/texture_handler.c` - Request handlers (lines 1-400)\n- `services/texture-service/CMakeLists.txt` - Build configuration (lines 1-248)\n\n### Configuration/Common\n- `libs/sc_common/include/sc_config.h` - Configuration framework (lines 1-303)\n- `docs/architecture/data_flow.puml` - Architecture diagram (lines 1-172)\n- `docs/architecture/overview.md` - System overview (lines 1-299)\n- `docs/architecture/microservices.md` - Microservices documentation (lines 1-572)\n\n---\n\n*Report prepared based on codebase analysis of SynestheticCanvas API Suite v1.4.x*\n",

# Technical Report: Migration from Custom IPC to gRPC

## Executive Summary

This report provides a comprehensive architectural analysis of the SynestheticCanvas API Suite's inter-service communication system and outlines a phased migration plan from the current hybrid IPC/HTTP approach to gRPC. The analysis is based on examination of the codebase, including the `sc_ipc` library, API Gateway, microservices, and build configuration files.

---

## 1. Component Identification

### 1.1 Current Inter-Service Communication Components

The SynestheticCanvas system uses a **hybrid communication approach**:

1. **UNIX Domain Socket IPC Library (`sc_ipc`)** - for local inter-process communication
2. **HTTP/REST over libcurl** - for network-based service-to-service calls

#### Core IPC Library Files

| File | Purpose |
|------|---------|
| `libs/sc_ipc/include/sc_ipc.h` | Public API header defining the IPC interface, message types, error codes, and envelope structures |
| `libs/sc_ipc/src/sc_ipc.c` | Implementation of UNIX domain socket-based IPC with length-prefixed framing |

#### API Gateway Client-Side Communication

| File | Purpose |
|------|---------|
| `api-gateway/src/services/service_client.c` | HTTP/REST client wrapper using libcurl for communicating with downstream microservices |
| `api-gateway/graphql/resolvers.c` | GraphQL resolvers that invoke `service_client` to call backend services |
| `api-gateway/src/main.c` | Gateway entry point and HTTP server initialization |
| `api-gateway/src/gateway_server.c` | HTTP server implementation |

#### Microservice Server-Side Components

| Service | Main Files |
|---------|-----------|
| **texture-service** | `services/texture-service/src/main.c` - HTTP daemon using libmicrohttpd |
| | `services/texture-service/src/texture_ha
